# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repository:** `github.com/sg-evals/kafka--0753c489`
- Use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kafka--0753c489$` filter in keyword_search
- Use `github.com/sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` as the `repo` parameter for go_to_definition/find_references/read_file


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Data Flow Q&A: Kafka Message Lifecycle

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/kafka--0753c489 (mirror of apache/kafka)
**Task Type:** Data Flow Q&A (investigation only — no code changes)

## Background

Apache Kafka is a distributed event streaming platform where messages flow from producers through brokers to consumers. Understanding this end-to-end message lifecycle — including every transformation, buffering, and persistence step — is essential for working with Kafka's architecture.

## Task

Trace the complete path of a single message from the moment a producer calls `send()` through broker persistence and replication, to final delivery to a consumer via `poll()`. Identify every key transformation point, component boundary crossing, and state change.

## Questions

Answer ALL of the following questions about Kafka's message lifecycle:

### Q1: Producer-Side Batching and Transmission

When a producer calls `KafkaProducer.send(record)`, how does the message travel from application code to the network?

- What is the role of `RecordAccumulator` in batching messages?
- How does the `Sender` thread determine when a batch is ready to transmit?
- What triggers the actual network request to the broker?
- At what point are messages serialized and assigned to partitions?

### Q2: Broker-Side Append and Replication

When a produce request arrives at the broker, how is the message written to disk and replicated?

- Which component receives the produce request and routes it to the correct partition leader?
- How does `ReplicaManager` coordinate the append operation?
- What is the sequence of operations that writes the message to the local log?
- How does the broker replicate the message to follower replicas before acknowledging the producer?

### Q3: Consumer-Side Fetch and Delivery

When a consumer calls `poll()`, how does it retrieve messages from the broker?

- How does the `Fetcher` component build and send fetch requests?
- What happens when fetch responses arrive from the broker?
- How are messages deserialized and delivered to application code?
- At what point do offset commits occur relative to message delivery?

### Q4: End-to-End Transformation Points

Identify all transformation points in the message lifecycle where data format or representation changes:

- Where does serialization occur (producer-side)?
- Where does the message get wrapped in protocol-level framing (RecordBatch)?
- Where is the message persisted to disk on the broker?
- Where does deserialization occur (consumer-side)?

List these transformation points in order and explain what changes at each step.

## Output Requirements

Write your answer to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with the following structure:

```
# Kafka Message Lifecycle

## Q1: Producer-Side Batching and Transmission
<answer with specific file paths, class names, and method references>

## Q2: Broker-Side Append and Replication
<answer with specific file paths, class names, and method references>

## Q3: Consumer-Side Fetch and Delivery
<answer with specific file paths, class names, and method references>

## Q4: End-to-End Transformation Points
<ordered list of transformation points with file/method references>

## Evidence
<consolidated list of supporting file paths and line references>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT modify any source files
- Cite specific files, classes, and methods — avoid vague or speculative answers
- Focus on the core message path, not error handling or edge cases
- Trace a single non-transactional message with acks=all (full replication)

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive investigation of the Apache Kafka message lifecycle. Here's what I've documented:

## Summary

I've created `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with detailed answers to all four questions:

### **Q1: Producer-Side Batching and Transmission**
- Traced the flow from `KafkaProducer.send()` through serialization (key/value), partition assignment
- Explained `RecordAccumulator` batching mechanism and how batches become ready for transmission
- Detailed the `Sender` thread's role in draining batches and sending `ProduceRequest`s to brokers

### **Q2: Broker-Side Append and Replication**
- Mapped how `KafkaApis.handleProduceRequest()` routes records to `ReplicaManager`
- Explained `UnifiedLog.appendAsLeaderWithRecordVersion()` that writes to persistent log segments
- Detailed replication coordination including `DelayedProduce` waiting for ISR acknowledgments
- Covered the response callback mechanism that sends `ProduceResponse` back to producer

### **Q3: Consumer-Side Fetch and Delivery**
- Traced `Fetcher.sendFetches()` creating `FetchRequest`s and sending to brokers
- Explained broker-side `DelayedFetch` reading from logs via `ReplicaManager`
- Detailed `FetchCollector.collectFetch()` parsing `RecordBatch` objects from `MemoryRecords`
- Described deserialization flow converting binary records to `ConsumerRecord<K, V>` objects
- Covered offset tracking and commit mechanism

### **Q4: End-to-End Transformation Points** (9 stages)
1. **Producer serialization** (objects → bytes)
2. **Batch encoding** (bytes → RecordBatch format)
3. **Network transmission** (RecordBatch → protocol frames)
4. **Broker unpacking** (protocol → per-partition MemoryRecords)
5. **Persistent storage** (memory → disk log segments)
6. **Fetch response** (log storage → p

  "content": "# Kafka Message Lifecycle\n\n## Q1: Producer-Side Batching and Transmission\n\nWhen a producer calls `KafkaProducer.send(record)`, the message travels through several stages before reaching the network:\n\n### Serialization and Partition Assignment\n- **Entry point**: `KafkaProducer.send(ProducerRecord, Callback)` in `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/KafkaProducer.java:941`\n- The record is first passed through interceptors via `ProducerInterceptor.onSend()` (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/ProducerInterceptor.java:42-45`)\n- The key and value are serialized independently using configured serializers:\n  - Key serialization at line 999: `keySerializerPlugin.get().serialize(record.topic(), record.headers(), record.key())`\n  - Value serialization at line 1007: `valueSerializerPlugin.get().serialize(record.topic(), record.headers(), record.value())`\n- Partition assignment occurs via `partition()` method (line 1017) which uses the configured partitioner (default: `BuiltInPartitioner` in `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/BuiltInPartitioner.java`)\n\n### Batching in RecordAccumulator\n- **RecordAccumulator role**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java:68` - \"This class acts as a queue that accumulates records into MemoryRecords instances to be sent to the server\"\n- Message is appended to accumulator via `accumulator.append()` (line 1029-1030):\n  - Method signature: `RecordAccumulator.append(String topic, int partition, long timestamp, byte[] key, byte[] value, Header[] headers, AppendCallbacks callbacks, long maxTimeToBlock, long nowMs, Cluster cluster)` at line 275\n- The append process (lines 294-358):\n  1. Determines effective partition based on partition info and broker availability\n  2. Attempts to append to existing in-flight batch via `tryAppend()` (line 319)\n  3. If batch is full or doesn't exist, allocates new buffer from buffer pool (line 333)\n  4. Creates new `ProducerBatch` with `MemoryRecordsBuilder` (line 394): `ProducerBatch(new TopicPartition(topic, partition), recordsBuilder, nowMs)`\n  5. Appends record to batch via `ProducerBatch.tryAppend()` which writes the serialized key/value to a `MemoryRecordsBuilder`\n\n### Record Batching Format\n- **Batch creation**: `RecordAccumulator.appendNewBatch()` at line 375\n- Records are grouped using `ProducerBatch` which wraps a `MemoryRecordsBuilder` (line 393)\n- `MemoryRecordsBuilder` encodes records in the current record format (MAGIC value) with:\n  - Record batch header metadata\n  - Compression codec settings\n  - Timestamp information\n  - Producer ID and sequence numbers (if idempotent/transactional)\n\n### Sender Thread and Network Transmission\n- **Sender thread class**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java:79` - \"The background thread that handles the sending of produce requests to the Kafka cluster\"\n- **Main sender loop**: `Sender.runOnce()` at line 305\n- **Producer data sending**: `sendProducerData()` at line 357:\n  1. Calls `accumulator.ready(metadataSnapshot, now)` (line 360) to identify partitions with ready batches\n  2. Returns list of ready nodes that have batches ready for transmission\n  3. Calls `accumulator.drain(metadataSnapshot, result.readyNodes, this.maxRequestSize, now)` (line 395) to extract batches from accumulator\n- **Ready criteria**: Batches become ready when:\n  - Batch size threshold is reached (determined by `batch.size` config), OR\n  - Linger time expires (determined by `linger.ms` config), OR\n  - Producer is flushed\n\n### Network Request Creation and Transmission\n- **Produce requests**: `Sender.sendProduceRequests()` at line 856 sends collated batches\n- For each ready node, a `ProduceRequest` is created containing:\n  - Required acknowledgments (`acks` setting: 0, 1, or -1 for all)\n  - Timeout value\n  - TopicPartition \u2192 MemoryRecords mapping (batches)\n- **Client send**: Via `KafkaClient.send()` which queues the request for network transmission\n- **Batch state**: Once sent, batch is moved to in-flight tracking via `addToInflightBatches()` (line 396)\n\n### Callback Mechanism\n- **AppendCallbacks**: Wrapper class at line 1558 in KafkaProducer that coordinates:\n  - Producer interceptor callbacks\n  - User-provided callback\n  - Future metadata updates when batch completes\n- **Batch completion**: `ProducerBatch.complete(baseOffset, logAppendTime)` at line 218 or `completeExceptionally()` at line 231 fires all callbacks\n\n---\n\n## Q2: Broker-Side Append and Replication\n\nWhen a produce request arrives at the broker, it is processed through several layers:\n\n### Request Routing\n- **KafkaApis handler**: `core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/KafkaApis.scala:388` - `handleProduceRequest(request: RequestChannel.Request, requestLocal: RequestLocal)`\n- Extracts `ProduceRequest` from request body (line 389)\n- Performs authorization checks and validates records (lines 391-442)\n- Routes authorized records to appropriate partitions in a map: `topicIdToPartitionData`\n\n### Replica Manager Coordination\n- **Append entry point**: `KafkaApis` calls `ReplicaManager.appendRecords()` or `ReplicaManager.appendRecordsToLeader()` (line 627 in `core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/ReplicaManager.scala`)\n- **Method signature** (line 674-682):\n  ```\n  def appendRecords(timeout: Long, requiredAcks: Short, internalTopicsAllowed: Boolean,\n                    origin: AppendOrigin, entriesPerPartition: Map[TopicIdPartition, MemoryRecords],\n                    responseCallback: Map[TopicIdPartition, PartitionResponse] => Unit, ...)\n  ```\n\n### Local Log Append\n- **Local append execution**: `ReplicaManager.appendToLocalLog()` at line 1370\n- For each TopicPartition:\n  1. Gets partition via `getPartitionOrException(topicIdPartition)` (line 1407)\n  2. Calls `Partition.appendRecordsToLeader()` which delegates to `UnifiedLog.appendAsLeader()`\n- **UnifiedLog append**: `storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/UnifiedLog.java:104` and line 1040\n  - Method: `UnifiedLog.appendAsLeaderWithRecordVersion(MemoryRecords records, int leaderEpoch, RecordVersion recordVersion)`\n  - Calls internal `append()` method which:\n    1. Validates records using `LogValidator` (converts record formats if needed)\n    2. Assigns offsets to records\n    3. Writes records to current active `LogSegment`\n    4. Updates in-memory index structures\n    5. Returns `LogAppendInfo` containing: first offset, last offset, timestamps, etc.\n\n### Replication Coordination\n- **Replication model**: After local append, broker coordinates replication based on `requiredAcks`:\n  - **acks=0**: No acknowledgment required; response sent immediately before replication\n  - **acks=1**: Only leader acknowledgment required; response sent after local log append\n  - **acks=-1 (all)**: Wait for in-sync replicas (ISR) to acknowledge before responding\n- **Delayed produce handling**: For `acks=-1`, `ReplicaManager.maybeAddDelayedProduce()` creates a `DelayedProduce` operation\n  - Class: `core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/DelayedProduce.scala:57`\n  - Waits for `DelayedOperation.onComplete()` callback which fires when:\n    1. Required ISR count acknowledges the append, OR\n    2. Timeout expires\n  - Upon completion, `sendResponseCallback` is invoked with final `PartitionResponse` status\n\n### Follower Replication\n- **ReplicaFetcher threads**: `core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/ReplicaFetcher.scala` fetch data from leader\n- Each follower broker runs fetch requests to the leader for assigned partitions\n- Fetched data is appended locally via `ReplicaManager.appendRecordsToFollower()`\n- Follower updates its replica state and sends acknowledgment to leader\n- Leader tracks ISR membership and updates high watermark when replicas acknowledge\n\n### Response Callback\n- **sendResponseCallback**: Closure defined at line 449 in `KafkaApis.scala`\n- Merges responses from all partitions (authorized, unauthorized, non-existing, invalid)\n- Applies quota throttling if needed (lines 484-495)\n- Sends `ProduceResponse` containing:\n  - For each partition: partition index, error code, base offset, log append timestamp\n  - If `acks=0`, sent immediately without waiting for replication\n\n---\n\n## Q3: Consumer-Side Fetch and Delivery\n\nWhen a consumer calls `poll()`, it retrieves messages through the following stages:\n\n### Fetch Request Preparation and Sending\n- **Consumer poll entry point**: `KafkaConsumer.poll(Duration timeout)`\n- Internally calls `ClassicKafkaConsumer.poll()` which:\n  1. Calls `pollForFetches(timer)` at line 690 in `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ClassicKafkaConsumer.java`\n  2. Calls `Fetcher.sendFetches()` at line 105 in `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/Fetcher.java`\n\n- **Fetch request creation**: `Fetcher.sendFetches()` and `sendFetchesInternal()` (line 184):\n  1. Calls `prepareFetchRequests()` to build map of Node \u2192 FetchRequestData for assigned partitions\n  2. For each partition: includes current fetch offset, max bytes to fetch, isolation level\n  3. Creates `FetchRequest.Builder` via `createFetchRequest(fetchTarget, data)` (line 192)\n  4. Sends to each node via `client.send(fetchTarget, request)` (line 193)\n  5. Attaches success/failure handlers that call `handleFetchSuccess()` or `handleFetchFailure()`\n\n### Broker-Side Fetch Processing\n- **KafkaApis fetch handler**: `core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/KafkaApis.scala:555` - `handleFetchRequest(request: RequestChannel.Request)`\n- Extracts `FetchRequest` and creates fetch context\n- Validates authorization and partition existence for requested partitions\n- **Delayed fetch**: Creates `DelayedFetch` operation via `ReplicaManager.readFromLog()` (line 171 in `core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/DelayedFetch.scala`)\n- Reads records from `UnifiedLog.readUncommitted()` or `readCommitted()` based on isolation level\n- Returns records as `LogReadResult` containing:\n  - Fetched `MemoryRecords` (encoded record batches)\n  - High watermark\n  - Log start offset\n  - Aborted transactions (for transactional reads)\n\n### Fetch Response Processing\n- **Success handler**: `Fetcher.handleFetchSuccess()` in `AbstractFetch`\n- Receives `ClientResponse` containing `FetchResponse` with MemoryRecords per partition\n- Stores response in `FetchBuffer` as `CompletedFetch` objects (each contains FetchResponseData.PartitionData with MemoryRecords)\n\n### Record Deserialization and Collection\n- **FetchCollector class**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/FetchCollector.java:51`\n- **collectFetch()** method (line 92):\n  1. Iterates through `CompletedFetch` objects in `FetchBuffer`\n  2. For each fetch, calls `initialize(completedFetch)` (line 109) which:\n     - Calls `handleInitializeSuccess()` (line 228)\n     - Returns initialized `CompletedFetch`\n  3. Calls `fetchRecords(nextInLineFetch, recordsRemaining)` (line 133):\n     - Validates partition is still assigned and fetchable\n     - Extracts current fetch position from subscription state\n     - Calls `CompletedFetch.fetchRecords(fetchConfig, deserializers, maxRecords)` (line 170)\n\n- **Record deserialization**: Within `CompletedFetch.fetchRecords()`:\n  1. Iterates through `RecordBatch` objects in the `MemoryRecords`\n  2. For each `RecordBatch`:\n     - Validates batch magic version and format\n     - Iterates through individual `Record` objects\n     - Deserializes key using configured key deserializer\n     - Deserializes value using configured value deserializer\n     - Creates `ConsumerRecord<K, V>` object with:\n       - Topic, partition, offset\n       - Timestamp and timestamp type\n       - Headers\n       - Deserialized key and value\n       - LeaderEpoch\n       - SerializedKeySize, SerializedValueSize\n  3. Updated after records are returned to track next fetch offset\n- **Explicit commit**: Consumer calls `commitSync()` or `commitAsync()` which:\n  - Invokes `CommitRequestManager` to send `OffsetCommit` request to group coordinator\n  - Returns `LogAppendInfo` containing: first offset, last offset, timestamps, etc.\n\n### Replication Coordination\n- **Replication model**: After local append, broker coordinates replication based on `requiredAcks`:\n  - **acks=0**: No acknowledgment required; response sent immediately before replication\n  - **acks=1**: Only leader acknowledgment required; response sent after local log append\n  - **acks=-1 (all)**: Wait for in-sync replicas (ISR) to acknowledge before responding\n- **Delayed produce handling**: For `acks=-1`, `ReplicaManager.maybeAddDelayedProduce()` creates a `DelayedProduce` operation\n  - Class: `core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/DelayedProduce.scala:57`\n  - Waits for `DelayedOperation.onComplete()` callback which fires when:\n    1. Required ISR count acknowledges the append, OR\n    2. # Kafka Message Lifecycle

## Q1: Producer-Side Batching and Transmission

When a producer calls `KafkaProducer.send(record)`, the message travels through several stages before reaching the network:

### Serialization and Partition Assignment
- **Entry point**: `KafkaProducer.send(ProducerRecord, Callback)` in `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/KafkaProducer.java:941`
- The record is first passed through interceptors via `ProducerInterceptor.onSend()` (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/ProducerInterceptor.java:42-45`)
- The key and value are serialized independently using configured serializers:
  - Key serialization at line 999: `keySerializerPlugin.get().serialize(record.topic(), record.headers(), record.key())`
  - Value serialization at line 1007: `valueSerializerPlugin.get().serialize(record.topic(), record.headers(), record.value())`
- Partition assignment occurs via `partition()` method (line 1017) which uses the configured partitioner (default: `BuiltInPartitioner` in `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/BuiltInPartitioner.java`)

### Batching in RecordAccumulator
- **RecordAccumulator role**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java:68` - "This class acts as a queue that accumulates records into MemoryRecords instances to be sent to the server"
- Message is appended to accumulator via `accumulator.append()` (line 1029-1030):
  - Method signature: `RecordAccumulator.append(String topic, int partition, long timestamp, byte[] key, byte[] value, Header[] headers, AppendCallbacks callbacks, long maxTimeToBlock, long nowMs, Cluster cluster)` at line 275
- The append process (lines 294-358):
  1. Determines effective partition based on partition
